</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Labor" title="Template:Labor"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Labor" title="Template talk:Labor"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Labor&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Employment</b> is a relationship between two <a href="/wiki/Party_(law)" title="Party (law)">parties</a> <a href="/wiki/Regulation" title="Regulation">regulating</a> the provision of paid labour services.  Usually based on a <a href="/wiki/Employment_contract" title="Employment contract">contract</a>, one party, the employer, which might be a <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">corporation</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Not-for-profit_organization" title="Not-for-profit organization">not-for-profit organization</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-operative" title="Co-operative">co-operative</a>, or any other entity, pays the other, the employee, in return for carrying out assigned work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-1">[1]</a></sup> Employees work in return for wages, which can be paid on the basis of an hourly rate, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piecework" title="Piecework">piecework</a> or an annual <a href="/wiki/Salary" title="Salary">salary</a>, depending on the type of work an employee does, the prevailing conditions of the sector and the <a href="/wiki/Bargaining_power" title="Bargaining power">bargaining power</a> between the parties. Employees in some sectors may receive <a href="/wiki/Gratuity" title="Gratuity">gratuities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonus_payment" title="Bonus payment">bonus payments</a> or <a href="/wiki/Employee_stock_option" title="Employee stock option">stock options</a>. In some types of employment, employees may receive benefits in addition to payment. Benefits may include <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Housing" title="Housing">housing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disability_insurance" title="Disability insurance">disability insurance</a>. Employment is typically governed by <a href="/wiki/Labour_law" title="Labour law">employment laws</a>, organisation or legal contracts.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Employees_and_employers"><span class="anchor" id="Employee"></span> Employees and employers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Employees and employers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Supervisor" title="Supervisor">Supervisor</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_employers" title="List of largest employers">List of largest employers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_professions" title="List of professions">List of professions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tradesman" title="Tradesman">Tradesman</a></div>
<p>An <b>employee</b> contributes labour and expertise to an endeavor of an <b>employer</b> or of a person conducting a business or undertaking (PCB)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and is usually hired to perform specific duties which are packaged into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Job_(role)" title="Job (role)">job</a>. In a corporate context, an employee is a person who is hired to provide services to a <a href="/wiki/Company" title="Company">company</a> on a regular basis in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Financial_compensation" title="Financial compensation">compensation</a> and who does not provide these services as part of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_business" title="Independent business">independent business</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_contractor">Independent contractor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Independent contractor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This section is about the classification in general. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Independent_contractor_(disambiguation)" title="Independent contractor (disambiguation)">Independent contractor (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p>An issue that arises in most companies, especially the ones that are in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gig_economy" title="Gig economy">gig economy</a>, is the classification of workers. A lot of workers that fulfill gigs are often hired as <i>independent contractors</i>.
</p><p>To categorize a worker as an independent contractor rather than an employee, an independent contractor must agree with the client on what the finished work product will be and then the contractor controls the means and manner of achieving the desired outcome. Secondly, an independent contractor offers services to the public at large, not just to one business, and is responsible for disbursing payments from the client, paying unreimbursed expenses, and providing his or her own tools to complete the job. Third, the relationship of the parties is often evidenced by a written agreement that specifies that the worker is an independent contractor and is not entitled to employee benefits; the services provided by the worker are not key to the business; and the relationship is not permanent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-author_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-author-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>As a general principle of employment law, in the United States, there is a difference between an agent and an independent contractor. The default status of a worker is an employee unless specific guidelines are met, which can be determined by the ABC test.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Thus, clarifying whether someone who performs work is an independent contractor or an employee from the beginning, and treating them accordingly, can save a company from trouble later on.
</p><p>Provided key circumstances, including ones such as that the worker is paid regularly, follows set hours of work, is supplied with tools from the employer, is closely monitored by the employer, acting on behalf of the employer, only works for one employer at a time, they are considered an employee,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and the employer will generally be liable for their actions and be obliged to give them benefits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Similarly, the employer is the owner of any invention created by an employee “hired to invent,” even in the absence of an assignment of inventions. In contrast, a company commissioning a work by an independent contractor will not own the copyright unless the company secures either a written contract stating that it is a “work made for hire” or a written assignment of the copyright. In order to stay protected and avoid lawsuits, an employer has to be aware of that distinction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-author_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-author-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Employer.E2.80.93worker_relationship"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Employer–worker_relationship">Employer–worker relationship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Employer–worker relationship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Employer and managerial control within an organization rests at many levels and has important implications for staff and productivity alike, with control forming the fundamental link between desired outcomes and actual processes. Employers must balance interests such as decreasing wage constraints with a maximization of labor productivity in order to achieve a profitable and productive employment relationship.
</p>
<h3><span id="Labor_acquisition_.2F_hiring"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_acquisition_/_hiring">Labor acquisition / hiring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Labor acquisition / hiring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Application_for_employment" title="Application for employment">Application for employment</a></div>
<p>The main ways for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Employer" title="Employer">employers</a> to find workers and for people to find employers are via jobs listings in newspapers (via <a href="/wiki/Classified_advertising" title="Classified advertising">classified advertising</a>) and online, also called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Job_board" title="Job board">job boards</a>. Employers and job seekers also often find each other via professional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recruitment_consultant" title="Recruitment consultant">recruitment consultants</a> which receive a <a href="/wiki/Commission_(remuneration)" title="Commission (remuneration)">commission</a> from the employer to find, screen and select suitable candidates. However, a study has shown that such consultants may not be reliable when they fail to use established principles in selecting employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-1">[1]</a></sup> A more traditional approach is with a "Help Wanted" <a href="/wiki/Sign" title="Sign">sign</a> in the establishment (usually hung on a window or door<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> or placed on a store counter).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-3">[3]</a></sup>  Evaluating different employees can be quite laborious but setting up different techniques to analyze their skills to measure their talents within the field can be best through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_%26_Organizational_Assessment" title="Industrial &amp; Organizational Assessment">assessments</a>.  Employer and potential employee commonly take the additional step of getting to know each other through the process of a <a href="/wiki/Job_interview" title="Job interview">job interview</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_and_development">Training and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Training and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki-training_with_employees_of_Regional_Institute_of_Culture_in_Katowice_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="636" data-file-width="958" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Wiki-training_with_employees_of_Regional_Institute_of_Culture_in_Katowice_02.jpg/220px-Wiki-training_with_employees_of_Regional_Institute_of_Culture_in_Katowice_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Wiki-training_with_employees_of_Regional_Institute_of_Culture_in_Katowice_02.jpg/330px-Wiki-training_with_employees_of_Regional_Institute_of_Culture_in_Katowice_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Wiki-training_with_employees_of_Regional_Institute_of_Culture_in_Katowice_02.jpg/440px-Wiki-training_with_employees_of_Regional_Institute_of_Culture_in_Katowice_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiki-training_with_employees_of_Regional_Institute_of_Culture_in_Katowice_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wiki-training with employees of Regional Institute of Culture in Katowice 02</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Training_and_development" title="Training and development">Training and development</a> refers to the employer's effort to equip a newly hired employee with the necessary skills to perform at the job, and to help the employee grow within the organization.  An appropriate level of training and development helps to improve employee's <a href="/wiki/Job_satisfaction" title="Job satisfaction">job satisfaction</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Remuneration">Remuneration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Remuneration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are many ways that employees are paid, including by hourly wages, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piecework" title="Piecework">piecework</a>, by yearly <a href="/wiki/Salary" title="Salary">salary</a>, or by <a href="/wiki/Gratuity" title="Gratuity">gratuities</a> (with the latter often being combined with another form of payment). In sales jobs and real estate positions, the employee may be paid a <a href="/wiki/Commission_(remuneration)" title="Commission (remuneration)">commission</a>, a percentage of the value of the goods or services that they have sold. In some fields and professions (<i>e.g.</i>, executive jobs), employees may be eligible for a bonus if they meet certain targets. Some executives and employees may be paid in <a href="/wiki/Share_capital" title="Share capital">shares</a> or <a href="/wiki/Employee_stock_option" title="Employee stock option">stock options</a>, a compensation approach that has the added benefit, from the company's point of view, of helping to align the interests of the compensated individual with the performance of the company.
</p><p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Faithless_servant" title="Faithless servant">faithless servant</a> doctrine, a <a href="/wiki/Legal_doctrine" title="Legal doctrine">doctrine</a> under the laws of a number of states in the United States, and most notably <a href="/wiki/Law_of_New_York_(state)" title="Law of New York (state)">New York State law</a>, an employee who acts unfaithfully towards his employer must forfeit all of the compensation he received during the period of his disloyalty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto6_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto6-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto5_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto5-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employee_benefits">Employee benefits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Employee benefits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Employee_benefits" title="Employee benefits">Employee benefits</a> are various non-wage compensation provided to employees in addition to their wages or salaries.  The benefits can include:  housing (employer-provided or employer-paid), group insurance (health, dental, life etc.), disability income protection, retirement benefits, daycare, tuition reimbursement, sick leave, vacation (paid and non-paid), social security, profit sharing, funding of education, and other specialized benefits. In some cases, such as with workers employed in remote or isolated regions, the benefits may include meals.  Employee benefits can improve the relationship between employee and employer and lowers staff turnover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizational_justice">Organizational justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Organizational justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Organizational_justice" title="Organizational justice">Organizational justice</a> is an employee's perception and judgement of employer's treatment in the context of fairness or justice.  The resulting actions to influence the employee-employer relationship is also a part of organizational justice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Workforce_organizing">Workforce organizing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Workforce organizing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Employees can organize into trade or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_union" title="Labor union">labor unions</a>, which represent the workforce to collectively bargain with the management of organizations about working, and contractual conditions and services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ending_employment">Ending employment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ending employment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Usually, either an employee or employer may end the relationship at any time, often subject to a certain notice period. This is referred to as <a href="/wiki/At-will_employment" title="At-will employment">at-will employment</a>. The contract between the two parties specifies the responsibilities of each when ending the relationship and may include requirements such as notice periods, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Severance_pay" title="Severance pay">severance pay</a>, and security measures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-17">[17]</a></sup> A contract forbidding an employee from leaving their employment, under penalty of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surety_bond" title="Surety bond">surety bond</a>, is referred to as an <a href="/wiki/Employment_bond" title="Employment bond">employment bond</a>. In some professions, notably teaching, civil servants, university professors, and some orchestra jobs, some employees may have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tenure" title="Tenure">tenure</a>, which means that they cannot be dismissed at will. Another type of termination is a <a href="/wiki/Layoff" title="Layoff">layoff</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wage_labor">Wage labor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Wage labor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wage_labor" title="Wage labor">Wage labor</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rebar_worker.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Rebar_worker.jpg/220px-Rebar_worker.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Rebar_worker.jpg/330px-Rebar_worker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Rebar_worker.jpg/440px-Rebar_worker.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rebar_worker.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Worker assembling <a href="/wiki/Rebar" title="Rebar">rebar</a> for a water treatment plant in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mazatlan" title="Mazatlan">Mazatlan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Wage labor is the <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomics" title="Socioeconomics">socioeconomic</a> relationship between a <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">worker</a> and an employer, where the worker sells their <a href="/wiki/Labour_economics" title="Labour economics">labor</a> under a formal or informal employment <a href="/wiki/Contract" title="Contract">contract</a>. These transactions usually occur in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_market" title="Labor market">labor market</a> where <a href="/wiki/Wage" title="Wage">wages</a> are market-determined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-:5-16">[16]</a></sup> In exchange for the wages paid, the work product generally becomes the <a href="/wiki/Work_for_hire" title="Work for hire">undifferentiated property</a> of the employer, except for special cases such as the vesting of <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_property" title="Intellectual property">intellectual property</a> patents in the United States where <a href="/wiki/Patent#Ownership" title="Patent">patent rights</a> are <a href="/wiki/Freelancer" title="Freelancer">usually</a> vested in the original personal inventor. A wage laborer is a person whose primary means of income is from the selling of his or her labor in this way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-:6-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>In modern mixed economies such as that of the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development#Current_members" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">countries</a>, it is currently the dominant form of work arrangement. Although most work occurs following this structure, the wage work arrangements of  <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEOs</a>, professional employees, and professional contract workers are sometimes conflated with <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">class assignments</a>, so that "wage labor" is considered to apply only to unskilled, semi-skilled or <a href="/wiki/Manual_labour" title="Manual labour">manual labor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geoffrey_Ostergaard_p._133_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geoffrey_Ostergaard_p._133-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wage_slavery">Wage slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Wage slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Labour_economics#Wage_slavery" title="Labour economics">Labour economics</a></div>
<p>Wage labor, as institutionalized under today's market economic systems, has been criticized,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-:6-17">[17]</a></sup> especially by both mainstream <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-syndicalism" title="Anarcho-syndicalism">anarcho-syndicalists</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geoffrey_Ostergaard_p._133_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Geoffrey_Ostergaard_p._133-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-English_Working_Class_p._599_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-English_Working_Class_p._599-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-English_Working_Class_p._912_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-English_Working_Class_p._912-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shop_Floor_p._37_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shop_Floor_p._37-21">[21]</a></sup> using the <a href="/wiki/Pejorative" title="Pejorative">pejorative</a> term <a href="/wiki/Wage_slavery" title="Wage slavery">wage slavery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-merriam-webster.com_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-merriam-webster.com-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Socialists draw parallels between the trade of <a href="/wiki/Wage_labour" title="Wage labour">labor</a> as a commodity and <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a> is also known to have suggested such parallels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>The American philosopher <a href="/wiki/John_Dewey" title="John Dewey">John Dewey</a> posited that until "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_exploitation" title="Economic exploitation">industrial feudalism</a>" is replaced by "<a href="/wiki/Industrial_democracy" title="Industrial democracy">industrial democracy</a>", politics will be "the shadow cast on society by big business".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Ferguson_(academic)" title="Thomas Ferguson (academic)">Thomas Ferguson</a> has postulated in his <a href="/wiki/Investment_theory_of_party_competition" title="Investment theory of party competition">investment theory of party competition</a> that the undemocratic nature of economic institutions under capitalism causes elections to become occasions when blocs of investors coalesce and compete to control the state plus cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-:7-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment_contract">Employment contract</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Employment contract">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Employment_contract" title="Employment contract">Employment contract</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Australian employment has been governed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fair_Work_Act" title="Fair Work Act">Fair Work Act</a> since 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bangladesh Association of International Recruiting Agencies (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BAIRA" title="BAIRA">BAIRA</a>) is an association of national level with its international reputation of co-operation and welfare of the migrant workforce as well as its approximately 1200 members agencies in collaboration with and support from the Government of Bangladesh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geoffrey_Ostergaard_p._133_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Geoffrey_Ostergaard_p._133-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">Canadian province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, formal complaints can be brought to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Labour_(Ontario)" title="Ministry of Labour (Ontario)">Ministry of Labour</a>. In the province of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, grievances can be filed with the <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20061011030434/http://www.cnt.gouv.qc.ca/en/index.asp" rel="nofollow">Commission des normes du travail</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shop_Floor_p._37_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shop_Floor_p._37-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two of the prominent examples of work and employment contracts in Germany are the <b>Werksvertrag</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> or the <b>Arbeitsvertrag</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> which is a form of Dienstleistungsvertrag (service-oriented contract). An Arbeitsvertrag can also be temporary,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> whereas a temporary worker is working under <b>Zeitarbeit</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> or <b>Leiharbeit</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Another employment setting is <b>Arbeitnehmerüberlassung</b> (ANÜ).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Labour_in_India" title="Labour in India">Labour in India</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> has options for a fixed term contract or a permanent contract. Both contracts are entitled to minimum wages, fixed working hours and social security contributions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shop_Floor_p._37_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-Shop_Floor_p._37-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> has no contract Labor, Minimum Wage and Provident Funds Acts. Contract labor in Pakistan must be paid minimum wage and certain facilities are to be provided to labor. However, the Acts are not yet fully implemented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geoffrey_Ostergaard_p._133_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-Geoffrey_Ostergaard_p._133-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, employment is regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Labor_and_Employment_(Philippines)" title="Department of Labor and Employment (Philippines)">Department of Labor and Employment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-:8-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to Swedish law,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> there are three types of employment.
</p>
<ul><li>Test employment (<i>swe: Provanställning</i>), where the employer hires a person for a test period of 6 months maximum. The employment can be ended at any time without giving any reason. This type of employment can be offered only once per employer and in employee combination. Usually, a time limited or normal employment is offered after a test employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>Time limited employment (<i>swe: Tidsbegränsad anställning</i>). The employer hires a person for a specified time. Usually, they are extended for a new period. Total maximum two years per employer and employee combination, then it automatically counts as a normal employment.</li>
<li>Normal employment (<i>swe: Tillsvidareanställning / Fast anställning</i>), which has no time limit (except for retirement etc.). It can still be ended for two reasons: <b>personal reason</b>, immediate end of employment only for strong reasons such as crime, or <b>lack of work tasks</b> (<i>swe: Arbetsbrist</i>), cancellation of employment, usually because of bad income for the company. There is a cancellation period of 1–6 months, and rules for how to select employees, basically those with shortest employment time shall be cancelled first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>There are no laws about <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum salary</a> in Sweden. Instead, there are agreements between employer organizations and trade unions about minimum salaries, and other employment conditions.
</p><p>There is a type of employment contract which is common but not regulated in law, and that is Hour employment (<i>swe: Timanställning</i>), which can be Normal employment (unlimited), but the work time is unregulated and decided per immediate need basis. The employee is expected to be answering the phone and come to work when needed, e.g. when someone is ill and absent from work. They will receive salary only for actual work time and can in reality be fired for no reason by not being called anymore. This type of contract is common in the public sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Callcentreterminal.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="687" data-file-width="916" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Callcentreterminal.JPG/200px-Callcentreterminal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Callcentreterminal.JPG/300px-Callcentreterminal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Callcentreterminal.JPG/400px-Callcentreterminal.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Callcentreterminal.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Call_centre" title="Call centre">call centre</a> worker confined to a small workstation/booth.</div></div></div>
<p>In the United Kingdom, employment contracts are categorized by the government into the following types:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fixed-term_contract" title="Fixed-term contract">Fixed-term contract</a>: last for a certain length of time, are set in advance, end when a specific task is completed, ends when a specific event takes place.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Full-time_job" title="Full-time job">Full-time</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Part-time_contract" title="Part-time contract">part-time contract</a>: has no defined length of time, can be terminated by either party, is to accomplish a specific task, specified number of hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-:8-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>Agency staff</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Freelancer" title="Freelancer">Freelancers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consultant" title="Consultant">Consultants</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_contractor" title="Independent contractor">Contractors</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zero-hour_contract" title="Zero-hour contract">Zero-hour contracts</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_States_labor_law" title="United States labor law">United States labor law</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_employers_in_the_United_States" title="List of largest employers in the United States">List of largest employers in the United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Labor_unions_in_the_United_States" title="Labor unions in the United States">Labor unions in the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EmploymentUSbranchFredgr.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="631" data-file-width="977" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/EmploymentUSbranchFredgr.png/220px-EmploymentUSbranchFredgr.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/EmploymentUSbranchFredgr.png/330px-EmploymentUSbranchFredgr.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/EmploymentUSbranchFredgr.png/440px-EmploymentUSbranchFredgr.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EmploymentUSbranchFredgr.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>All employees, private industries, by branches</div></div></div>
<p>For purposes of U.S. federal income tax withholding, 26 U.S.C. § 3401(c) provides a definition for the term "employee" specific to chapter 24 of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Code" title="Internal Revenue Code">Internal Revenue Code</a>:
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Government_employment_as_%25_of_total_employment_in_EU.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="661" data-file-width="843" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Government_employment_as_%25_of_total_employment_in_EU.jpg/220px-Government_employment_as_%25_of_total_employment_in_EU.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Government_employment_as_%25_of_total_employment_in_EU.jpg/330px-Government_employment_as_%25_of_total_employment_in_EU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Government_employment_as_%25_of_total_employment_in_EU.jpg/440px-Government_employment_as_%25_of_total_employment_in_EU.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Government_employment_as_%25_of_total_employment_in_EU.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Government employment as % of total employment in EU</div></div></div>
<p>"For purposes of this chapter, the term "employee" includes an officer, employee, or elected official of the United States, a State, or any political subdivision thereof, or the District of Columbia, or any agency or instrumentality of any one or more of the foregoing. The term "employee" also includes an officer of a corporation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> This definition does not exclude all those who are commonly known as 'employees'. "Similarly, Latham’s instruction which indicated that under 26 U.S.C. § 3401(c) the category of ‘employee’ does not include privately employed wage earners is a preposterous reading of the statute. It is obvious that within the context of both statutes the word ‘includes’ is a term of enlargement not of limitation, and the reference to certain entities or categories is not intended to exclude all others."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>Employees are often contrasted with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_contractors" title="Independent contractors">independent contractors</a>, especially when there is dispute as to the worker's entitlement to have matching taxes paid, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Workers_compensation" title="Workers compensation">workers compensation</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unemployment_insurance" title="Unemployment insurance">unemployment insurance</a> benefits. However, in September 2009, the court case of <i>Brown v. J. Kaz, Inc.</i> ruled that independent contractors are regarded as employees for the purpose of <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">discrimination laws</a> if they work for the employer on a regular basis, and said employer directs the time, place, and manner of employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-:8-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>In non-union work environments, in the United States, unjust termination complaints can be brought to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Labor" title="United States Department of Labor">United States Department of Labor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>Labor unions are legally recognized as representatives of workers in many industries in the United States.  Their activity today centers on <a href="/wiki/Collective_bargaining" title="Collective bargaining">collective bargaining</a> over wages, benefits, and working conditions for their membership, and on representing their members in disputes with management over violations of contract provisions. Larger unions also typically engage in lobbying activities and electioneering at the state and federal level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_40-3"><a href="#cite_note-:8-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most unions in America are aligned with one of two larger umbrella organizations: the <a href="/wiki/AFL%E2%80%93CIO" title="AFL–CIO">AFL–CIO</a> created in 1955, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Change_to_Win_Federation" title="Change to Win Federation">Change to Win Federation</a> which split from the AFL–CIO in 2005. Both advocate policies and legislation on behalf of workers in the United States and Canada, and take an active role in politics. The AFL–CIO is especially concerned with global trade issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-:7-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>American business theorist <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Pfeffer" title="Jeffrey Pfeffer">Jeffrey Pfeffer</a> posits that contemporary employment practices and employer commonalities in the United States, including toxic working environments, job insecurity, long hours and increased performance pressure from management, are responsible for 120,000 excess deaths annually, making the workplace the fifth leading cause of death in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Age-related_issues">Age-related issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Age-related issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Younger_age_workers">Younger age workers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Younger age workers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_youth_employment_rate,_both_genders.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/US_youth_employment_rate%2C_both_genders.png/220px-US_youth_employment_rate%2C_both_genders.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/US_youth_employment_rate%2C_both_genders.png/330px-US_youth_employment_rate%2C_both_genders.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/US_youth_employment_rate%2C_both_genders.png/440px-US_youth_employment_rate%2C_both_genders.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_youth_employment_rate,_both_genders.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Youth employment rate in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">US</a>, i.e. the ratio of employed persons (15–24Y) in an economy to total <a href="/wiki/Labor_force_in_the_United_States" title="Labor force in the United States">labor force</a> (15–24Y).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Young_worker_safety_and_health" title="Young worker safety and health">Young worker safety and health</a></div>
<p>Young workers are at higher risk for <a href="/wiki/Occupational_injury" title="Occupational injury">occupational injury</a> and face certain <a href="/wiki/Occupational_hazard" title="Occupational hazard">occupational hazards</a> at a higher rate; this is generally due to their employment in high-risk industries. For example, in the United States, young people are injured at work at twice the rate of their older counterparts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup> These workers are also at higher risk for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle_accidents" title="Motor vehicle accidents">motor vehicle accidents</a> at work, due to less work experience, a lower use of seat belts, and higher rates of distracted driving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> To mitigate this risk, those under the age of 17 are restricted from certain types of driving, including transporting people and goods under certain circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>High-risk industries for young workers include agriculture, restaurants, waste management, and mining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-50">[50]</a></sup> In the United States, those under the age of 18 are restricted from certain jobs that are deemed dangerous under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fair_Labor_Standards_Act" title="Fair Labor Standards Act">Fair Labor Standards Act</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-:1-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>Youth employment programs are most effective when they include both theoretical classroom training and hands-on training with work placements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the conversation of employment among younger aged workers, youth unemployment has also been monitored. <a href="/wiki/Youth_unemployment" title="Youth unemployment">Youth unemployment</a> rates tend to be higher than the adult rates in every country in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Older_age_workers">Older age workers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Older age workers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Those older than the statutory defined retirement age may continue to work, either out of enjoyment or necessity. However, depending on the nature of the job, older workers may need to transition into less-physical forms of work to avoid injury. Working past retirement age also has positive effects, because it gives a sense of purpose and allows people to maintain social networks and activity levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Older workers are often found to be discriminated against by employers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Working_poor">Working poor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Working poor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Worker,_Dhaka,_Bangladesh.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Worker%2C_Dhaka%2C_Bangladesh.jpg/220px-Worker%2C_Dhaka%2C_Bangladesh.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Worker%2C_Dhaka%2C_Bangladesh.jpg/330px-Worker%2C_Dhaka%2C_Bangladesh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Worker%2C_Dhaka%2C_Bangladesh.jpg/440px-Worker%2C_Dhaka%2C_Bangladesh.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Worker,_Dhaka,_Bangladesh.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A worker in <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Employment is no guarantee of escaping <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> (ILO) estimates that as many as 40% of workers are poor, not earning enough to keep their families above the $2 a day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> For instance, in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> most of the chronically poor are wage earners in formal employment, because their jobs are insecure and low paid and offer no chance to accumulate wealth to avoid risks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-4"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNRISD" title="UNRISD">UNRISD</a>, increasing labor productivity appears to have a negative impact on job creation: in the 1960s, a 1% increase in output per worker was associated with a reduction in employment growth of 0.07%, by the first decade of this century the same productivity increase implies reduced employment growth by 0.54%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-5"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> Both increased employment opportunities and increased labor productivity (as long as it also translates into higher wages) are needed to tackle poverty. Increases in employment without increases in productivity leads to a rise in the number of "working poor", which is why some experts are now promoting the creation of "quality" and not "quantity" in labor market policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-6"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> This approach does highlight how higher productivity has helped reduce poverty in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>, but the negative impact is beginning to show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-7"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, for example, employment growth has slowed while productivity growth has continued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-8"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> Furthermore, productivity increases do not always lead to increased wages, as can be seen in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, where the gap between productivity and wages has been rising since the 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-9"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>Researchers at the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Development_Institute" title="Overseas Development Institute">Overseas Development Institute</a> argue that there are differences across <a href="/wiki/Economic_sector" title="Economic sector">economic sectors</a> in creating employment that reduces poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-10"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> 24 instances of growth were examined, in which 18 reduced poverty. This study showed that other sectors were just as important in reducing <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-11"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Services_sector" title="Services sector">services sector</a> is most effective at translating productivity growth into employment growth. <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> provides a safety net for jobs and economic buffer when other sectors are struggling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-12"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Models_of_the_employment_relationship">Models of the employment relationship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Models of the employment relationship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Scholars conceptualize the employment relationship in various ways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> A key assumption is the extent to which the employment relationship necessarily includes conflicts of interests between employers and employees, and the form of such conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In economic theorizing, the labor market mediates all such conflicts such that employers and employees who enter into an employment relationship are assumed to find this arrangement in their own self-interest. In human resource management theorizing, employers and employees are assumed to have shared interests (or a unity of interests, hence the label “unitarism”). Any conflicts that exist are seen as a manifestation of poor human resource management policies or interpersonal clashes such as personality conflicts, both of which can and should be managed away. From the perspective of pluralist industrial relations, the employment relationship is characterized by a plurality of stakeholders with legitimate interests (hence the label “pluralism), and some conflicts of interests are seen as inherent in the employment relationship (e.g., wages v. profits). Lastly, the critical paradigm emphasizes antagonistic conflicts of interests between various groups (e.g., the competing capitalist and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Working_classes" title="Working classes">working classes</a> in a Marxist framework) that are part of a deeper social conflict of unequal power relations. As a result, there are four common models of employment:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>Mainstream economics: employment is seen as a mutually advantageous transaction in a free market between self-interested legal and economic equals</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Human_resource_management" title="Human resource management">Human resource management</a> (unitarism): employment is a long-term partnership of employees and employers with common interests</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Industrial_relations" title="Industrial relations">Pluralist industrial relations</a>: employment is a bargained exchange between stakeholders with some common and some competing economic interests and unequal bargaining power due to imperfect labor markets<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-14"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>Critical <a href="/wiki/Industrial_relations" title="Industrial relations">industrial relations</a>: employment is an unequal power relation between competing groups that is embedded in and inseparable from systemic inequalities throughout the socio-politico-economic system.</li></ol>
<p>These models are important because they help reveal why individuals hold differing perspectives on human resource management policies, labor unions, and employment regulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> For example, human resource management policies are seen as dictated by the market in the first view, as essential mechanisms for aligning the interests of employees and employers and thereby creating profitable companies in the second view, as insufficient for looking out for workers’ interests in the third view, and as manipulative managerial tools for shaping the ideology and structure of the workplace in the fourth view.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_literature">Academic literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Academic literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Literature on the employment impact of economic growth and on how growth is associated with employment at a macro, sector and industry level was aggregated in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-partnerplatform.org_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-partnerplatform.org-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>Researchers found evidence to suggest growth in manufacturing and services have good impact on employment. They found GDP growth on employment in agriculture to be limited, but that value-added growth had a relatively larger impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI2_42-15"><a href="#cite_note-ODI2-42">[42]</a></sup> The impact on job creation by industries/economic activities as well as the extent of the body of evidence and the key studies. For extractives, they again found extensive evidence suggesting growth in the sector has limited impact <a href="/wiki/John_Cena" title="John Cena">on</a> employment. In textiles, however, although evidence was low, studies suggest growth there positively contributed to job creation. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agri-business" title="Agri-business">agri-business</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, they found impact growth to be positive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-partnerplatform.org_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-partnerplatform.org-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>They found that most available literature focuses on <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Middle-income_countries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Middle-income countries (page does not exist)">middle-income countries</a> somewhat, where economic growth impact has been shown to be positive on employment. The researchers didn't find sufficient evidence to conclude any impact of growth on employment in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" title="Least developed country">LDCs</a> despite some pointing to the positive impact, others point to limitations. They recommended that complementary policies are necessary to ensure economic growth's positive impact on LDC employment. With trade, industry and investment, they only found limited evidence of positive impact on employment from industrial and investment policies and for others, while large bodies of evidence does exist, the exact impact remains contested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-partnerplatform.org_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-partnerplatform.org-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>Researchers have also explored the relationship between employment and illicit activities. Using evidence from Africa, a research team found that a program for Liberian ex-fighters reduced work hours on illicit activities. The employment program also reduced interest in mercenary work in nearby wars. The study concludes that while the use of capital inputs or cash payments for peaceful work created a reduction in illicit activities, the impact of training alone is rather low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Globalization_and_employment_relations">Globalization and employment relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Globalization and employment relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The balance of economic efficiency and social equity is the ultimate debate in the field of <a href="/wiki/Industrial_relations" title="Industrial relations">employment relations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-:9-62">[62]</a></sup> By meeting the needs of the employer; generating profits to establish and maintain economic efficiency; whilst maintaining a balance with the employee and creating social equity that benefits the worker so that he/she can fund and enjoy healthy living; proves to be a continuous revolving issue in westernized societies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-:9-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">Globalization</a> has affected these issues by creating certain economic factors that disallow or allow various employment issues. Economist Edward Lee (1996) studies the effects of globalization and summarizes the four major points of concern that affect employment relations:
</p>
<ol><li>International competition, from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newly_industrialized_countries" title="Newly industrialized countries">newly industrialized countries</a>, will cause unemployment growth and increased wage disparity for unskilled workers in industrialized countries. Imports from low-wage countries exert pressure on the manufacturing sector in industrialized countries and foreign direct investment (FDI) is attracted away from the industrialized nations, towards low-waged countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-:9-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>Economic liberalization will result in unemployment and wage inequality in developing countries. This happens as job losses in uncompetitive industries outstrip job opportunities in new industries.</li>
<li>Workers will be forced to accept worsening wages and conditions, as a global labor market results in a “race to the bottom”. Increased international competition creates a pressure to reduce the wages and conditions of workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-:9-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>Globalization reduces the autonomy of the nation state. Capital is increasingly mobile and the ability of the state to regulate economic activity is reduced.</li></ol>
<p>What also results from Lee's (1996) findings is that in industrialized countries an average of almost 70 per cent of workers are employed in the service sector, most of which consists of non-tradable activities. As a result, workers are forced to become more skilled and develop sought after trades, or find other means of survival. Ultimately this is a result of changes and trends of employment, an evolving <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">workforce</a>, and globalization that is represented by a more skilled and increasing highly diverse labor force, that are growing in non standard forms of employment (Markey, R. et al. 2006).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_62-4"><a href="#cite_note-:9-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternatives">Alternatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Alternatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subcultures">Subcultures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Subcultures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Various youth subcultures have been associated with not working, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hippie" title="Hippie">hippie</a> subculture in the 1960s and 1970s (which endorsed the idea of "dropping out" of society) and the <a href="/wiki/Punk_subculture" title="Punk subculture">punk subculture</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-secondary_education">Post-secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Post-secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the alternatives to work is engaging in post-secondary education at a <a href="/wiki/College" title="College">college</a>, <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Professional_school" title="Professional school">professional school</a>. One of the major costs of obtaining a post-secondary education is the <a href="/wiki/Opportunity_cost" title="Opportunity cost">opportunity cost</a> of forgone wages due to not working. At times when jobs are hard to find, such as during recessions, unemployed individuals may decide to get post-secondary education, because there is less of an opportunity cost.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_assistance">Social assistance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Social assistance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In some countries, individuals who are not working can receive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_assistance" title="Social assistance">social assistance</a> support (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Welfare" title="Welfare">welfare</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_Stamp_Program" title="Food Stamp Program">food stamps</a>) to enable them to rent housing, buy food, repair or replace household goods, maintenance of children and observe social customs that require financial expenditure.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Volunteerism">Volunteerism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Volunteerism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Workers who are not paid wages, such as <a href="/wiki/Volunteering" title="Volunteering">volunteers</a> who perform tasks for charities, hospitals or not-for-profit organizations, are generally not considered employed. One exception to this is an <a href="/wiki/Internship" title="Internship">internship</a>, an employment situation in which the worker receives training or experience (and possibly college credit) as the chief form of compensation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-:10-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indentured_servitude_and_slavery">Indentured servitude and slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Indentured servitude and slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Those who work under obligation for the purpose of fulfilling a debt, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">indentured servants</a>, or as property of the person or entity they work for, such as <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>, do not receive pay for their services and are not considered employed. Some historians<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2018)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> suggest that slavery is older than employment, but both arrangements have existed for all recorded history.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Indentured servitude and slavery are not considered<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2018)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> compatible with <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> or with <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-:10-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Employment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notes and references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">
